2017-12-30 21:51:39
Soumen D'Jones (The_Hungry_Nomad)
8943591
3.0
After a long time, your Hungry Nomad is back with his in depth reviews..!! ;)

Okay!! 

To start off with, Tibetan Delight.

As far as i remember, i visited Tibetan Delight some 10 days back. MAN!! This food hub never disappoints me. With uts lip smacking Roasted Chilli Pork, dry chilli chicken and its slurpy noodles...Tibetan Delight is indeed a delight for your taste buds...

Location : Near EXIDE crossing. You'll have to ask the locals for direction, because the place is not near the streets. It is located in a hidden lane, a very narrow one..which will make you a little uncomfy.

Food : The food is really good for the price list. They surely know how to cook meat. For it's a meat lovers paradise. You can get pork, lamb, chicken etc..I will definitely suggest their famous Roasted Dry Chilli Pork..with Hakka Egg Noodles.. delicious!!

Ambience : The ambience is pathetic.. No AC..Not properly lit..only fans and lanterns. Very poor seating arrangement. And most importantly, you have to visit this place during Monsoon or Winter...since this place can be a lil too sultry if you go on summer..In one word its a typical Tibetan Restaurant in the middle of Kolkata.

Staff : The staffs are very unprofessional. But they are polite and very kind people..I liked their service...fast and they are good listeners.

I have to mention this, that the Hygiene of the place is not upto the mark. So if you guys wanna pay a visit for its tasty meaty foods, they thumbs up. Youre good.

Hungry Nomad will rate this place.

Food : 3 / 5
Ambience : 2 / 5
Staff : 3 / 5

Overall : 3/5

Happy food hunting Nomads.

This place is situated in a very small alleyway. It was even hard with the Google map to trace this place atva go for the first time. Still, we managed to reach this place at the evening time on 28th Dec 2017. This tiny place can accomodate about 12 people at a time with its 4 table sitting arrangement. I could see that some people were sitting with their food outside which I found to be roadside sitting arrangement instead of outdoor arena. Anyway, we got a table for 3 of us in 20 minutes or so. The restaurant was dimly lit and there was only one serving person. The same person was taking the orders, cleaning the tables, bringing the food etc etc. We waiting some more time to provide our order. 
We ordered chicken steamed momo, pan fried chicken momo, Schezuan chicken noodles.
Steam momo was good but the momo covering seemed to be thick and overcooked. The pan fried momo was nothing like fried. It was the steam momo with a spicey sauce covering it. Still, the sauce was tasty and only one thing which I liked about this place. The Schezuan chicken noodles' dish was super spicey and full with some undercooked, hard green leaves which were irritating to chew. 
Overall the experience at this place was not nice at all. They should also consider the hygiene seriously. There must be some differences between a roadside food stall and a restaurant featured in Zomato.

Okay straightly coming to the review-
After post Christmas hangout,I & 3 other friends just rushed into Tibetian Delights with hunger Chinese food.
First thing,it's really hard to find the restaurant. It's actually in an alley to the opposite of P.C.Chandra Jwellers,Elgin. The alley is really narrowüòí
Secondly the restaurant is really small,it's actually 1 room place having 4 tables & 16 chairs. But still there was a good thing that the kitchen is not being overlapped with the sitting place so there was no smell or smoke of kitchen.
Now coming to food- We ordered chicken pan fried momo,Mixed haka noodles(without pork),schezwan noodles(non veg),Schezwan Chicken,Chicken in oyester sauce.
All the dishes were really really good,both in quality & taste,but if the Schezwan noodles was a little more spicy,it would be better.
Service was first. Prices were reasonable and if two or three people go together then it is very much pocket friendly.
So just don't go with location or space because food is really good and would love go again üòç

2017-12-10 17:43:10
Vivek Mukherjee
29089792
5.0
Taking about the food its just Lip Smacking .I call it "Fingerlicious" because u cant resist urself licking ur fingers. We went there late at about 9.10pm and they served us by 10mins hardly. My girlfriend also loved it. We were lost locating the place so the owner send their staff to receive us which was a great hospitality on their part. We both loved it. Ambience wise it is not so grand but just like other small eating joints and Chinese Eating House in Kolkata.

Tibetan Delight is one of the hidden gems among restaurants of Kolkata. It is located inside a narrow shabby lane which is very very hard to locate. The nearest landmark is HDFC bank and P.C. Chandra Jewellers. The lane is just opposite Rabindra Sadan Metro Gate no. 4 .Have to cross the road exiting metro and take zebra crossing and go to another side of the road near CHAI BREAK and then turn right to the footpath and take left for that narrow lane which is just opposite the HDFC BANK. If u have difficulty call the restaurant no and they will send their staff to receive u near metro gate.

##

2017-09-24 18:41:05
Arnab Chatterjee
31783977
3.5
This is a hard place to find if you are not accustomed to the area around Elgin Road . If you are walking towards Elgin Road from Exide Crossing cross Bhishop Lefroy Road first & then Suburban Hospital Road - continue walking & you will get a narrow lane ( non motorable ) on the left , once you enter this lane a signboard of Tibetan Delight will welcome you to the restaurant which is on the right hand side. It's a small joint with four tables & plastic chairs . The dimly lit room is decorated by hanging lamps . The lane itself is not very comfortable to walk & the situation worsens after a shower . 
Waiting time is a bit longer here . 
Coming to the food I ordered the following : 
Vegetable Chowmien Gravy : It lacked right quantity of salt & when I added a pinch a salt it became tasty. The gravy was quite good with adequate amount of vegetables . Quantity is sufficient for a person . 
Roast Chilli Pork : My favourite side dish with Chowmien . I asked to make it dry & they obliged . Pork was cooked nicely while the vegetables retained their crunchiness making it tasty . Quantity was again sufficient . 
Price is reasonable but one thing to be kept in mind that they do not accept cards , only cash .

##

2017-09-09 16:56:32
Anirban Halder
122104
3.0
The place is hard to locate though it is close to high road. You shall need precise directions to reach here.

The ambience is not impressive. There are four wooden tables with red top and red plastic chairs and Chinese lamps are hanging over the tables. The non-AC place is dingy and it seemed that to cover that up a bit, the lighting had been carefully planned. 
Because of the space crunch, you may have to share table with strangers. But, well, it has its loyal base of patrons and they don't come here for ambience or comfort but for good food.

I had heard good things about its pork dishes, so I ordered the red hot favourite of pork lovers- Roast Chilli Pork (Rs 160) and to go with it, Mixed Hakka Noodles (Rs 170). No tax is charged on food. The service was quick and the food reached in 11 mts. The portion of noodles was just enough for one. It had shrimps not prawns and in less amount. Chicken, pork and egg were in reasonable quantity and it tasted good. However, going by portion size vs price, I won't call it value for money. 

The Roast Chilli Pork had a lot more gravy than average serving and the pork pieces were swimming in it. It was desirably spicy and flavorful. The pork was cut out of slices and there were plenty of it. Unfortunately for me, it was lean meat and a little chewy hence. I like a bit fatty and tender pork. So, the meat bit was not satisfactory.

I would like to come back here for its steamed pork momo which are strongly recommended.

Particullarly for this one I was really disappointed. Momo was really bad. The whole outer cover was very slimy & undercooked. Even the stuffing was not well prepared. & the chutney along with the momo was bad too. But next we had "Mixed Hakka Chowmein" which was really good & lipsmacking. Silufficient portions of chicken, prawn & veggies made me feel good after the momo disaster. Along with hakka chow we had "Lemon Chicken". It was on a lighter mode. Tastes amazingly awsome with a significant presence of lemon slices. Goes well with spicy hakka chow.
Overall it was really good to be there & have thir amazing foods but their momo gave me a thud punch. Even roadside momos are far better than theirs. But except momos, each & every items were great.
Would love to visit againüíùüíù

2017-08-12 23:39:24
Shreya Gain
29529776
4.5
Tibetan Delight, as the name suggests, is indeed a delight for people who love to eat, and especially for those who are on a budget or broke. 

Located at a walkable distance from Rabindra Sadan metro station, this place is hard to find if you don't have someone accompanying who has been there earlier. Even Google maps fail at most times, such is the tricky location! It's located in a dingy lane, almost looks like a old school drug dealer's lane, and you'd get the vibe that you're there for some smuggling while walking through the dimly lit, narrow, dingy lane between two buildings. 

The place has almost no hygiene, which can be considered as the only con of the place. No AC either. There are barely four to five plastic tables with plastic chairs, each with a red Tibetan lamp over it. One can hardly see the other tables from their own table. 

Coming to the food, we ordered Mixed Hakka Noodles, Schezwan Noodles, and Hong Kong Chicken. The chicken dish had a white gravy along with medium, soft pieces of meat which came with vegetables. The Hakka noodles were very tasty with different kinds of meat present in them, and the Schezwan noodles were very spice and were a little sticky. I liked the Hakka noodles more. One plate of chicken and two plates of noodles would be sufficient for three people, if not eating lushly. 

The service was okay. They weren't too slow, and served us hot and fresh food.

The bill was nominal and to add to our joys, they did not charge anything extra than the prices mentioned on the menu card. 

If you can find the place, you're in for a secret world of authentic Tibetan food! 

Happy eating!

This tiny restaurant is located in a narrow dingy alley , a little away from Momo Plaza, on the left towards Hazra. So is the slice pork with mushroom, that has a white sauce base , and capsicum and onions in the gravy. The service here is fairly quick , but they might not always have the soft drink of your choice. Overall , a must visit restaurant for pork lovers in the city .

Inspite of the ambience, size, I absolutely love this place. The food is extremely pleasing and have the potential to uplift your mood in a moment. 
HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!

One of the hidden gems in the Elgin area, Tibetan Delight is for those people who want to have good old spicy Chinese and Tibetan at a pocket-friendly budget. A lane opposite the Elgin-Chowringhee P.C chandra leads to it, and the first impression is sure to make you rethink your decision.

But trust me, that shady place is one of the better Tibetan joints in the city! They give a generous (rather, too much) quantity and has a feel of the home-made comfort food. I have gone their quite a few times, and I love their Pork preparations, Hot Garlic Chicken, the Chopsuey and the Fried Rice. The momos aren't worth the hype, so if you're visiting this place, my recommendation will be to go with the pork dishes.

Overall is a nice place if you are looking for a good brunch!

2017-03-18 15:37:30
Sparsh Jain
36664032
4.5
This place is located in a narrow lane exactly opposite to my house. Yet, it took me 19 odd years to know about its existence. Such is the location of Tibetan Delight. It's truly a hidden gem of Kolkata. I first visited this place when an old friend took me here. It was a reunion of sorts, and hence I developed a soft corner in my heart for it. Since then, I've visited this place about 10 times over the course of two years. The place is a little cramped for space, but the decor is thrilling. A dimly lit room, with chinese lanterns hanging over the tables give you a feel of the magical Land of the Dragon. Their chinese and tibetan dishes are too good. I have ordered Garlic Chicken, hakka chowmein, chicken fried rice, fried chicken momos, American Chopsuey, Chilli Pork, Schezwan chicken and egg noodles here. The quantity and quality they offer is too good compared to the cheap rates at which the dishes are priced. They offer a huge quantity in each plate, and two people having normal apetites may find it hard to finish two dishes between themselves. Among these, the one dish I will strongly recommend is their Garlic Chicken. They serve eight huge, boneless pieces of chicken with a lot of thick gravy at an affordable price. The gravy leaves you licking your fingers. I customarily order this dish everytime I visit this place, and I've also ordered just this dish for take-away on numerous occasions. The fact that they don't charge taxes makes the meal even cheaper! Overall, this place tops my list of favourite go-to restaurants if you want to eat to your heart's content without burning a hole through your pocket !

If this continues, the restaurant will be forced to close in a year or so. I was a regular there for more than 4 years but now I don't go and will never go.

Now coming to the food,

We Ordered : Chicken Steamed momo, Chicken Thukpa and chicken Drumsticks.
Food Ordered For Takeaway : Chicken Pan fried momo, Chicken Fried Rice and Manchurian Chicken.

TASTE of the momo was average and the filling of chicken inside it was very less in amount..It was served with a tasteless soup.
CHICKEN thukpa was decent in taste.It was mild in flavour with lots of noodles,vegetables and boiled chicken pieces.
CHICKEN drumstick was deep fried and served with a hot sauce,though the batter was very thik.

These 3 dishes which we had in the restaurant were good.But we were very disappointed by the takeaway food.

Chicken Pan fried momo : It was tossed in a very spicy red sauce with almost no filling inside the momo.It tasted so hot that it was literally getting impossible to consume.
Chicken fried rice : Tasteless, Mushy rice with no seasoning, less amount of chicken and prepared with hell lot of Black pepper.It was disgusting.
Manchurian chicken : probably the only dish which was good.

Overall I thik it is very over hyped place regarding its standard.Prices are also on the higher side considering this place has no AC, where many other restaurants with all these facilities charge lesser amount than this restaurant. The menu card that is in zomato is the older one.. Not a good start to Pujor pet pujo....

3.5
Was hearing a lot about this place from my friends so today we decided to visit the place for lunch before a movie outing.

Location: Really hard to find,really slender lanes running in between restaurants and buildings all standing tall beside the small joint.

Type: Its not really a restaurant, its a rather walk in Chinese joint that serves mediocre quality food with pocket friendly rates.

Ambience: Not at all decorated like the other restaurants around it but it looks decent with the Chinese luv a lamps. Other than the lamps the place is not at all maintained at all with dust and spider webs dangling here and there on the walls. The tables were those normal plastic ones with no table decorations and the sauce variants kept on the table didn't looked good enough for trying. So for ambience 2 out of 5

Service: There are only four tables with a single waiter handling all the tables but inspite of this he does good service. For service 4 out of 5

Food Quality: We ordered a chicken soup which was good with huge amounts of chickens but the only thing that disappointed was the amount of black pepper that made it spicy but due to the rainy weather our friend who ordered it loved it. We didn't had time for starters so we decided to order the main course. The plates were really normal with no garnishing at all. We ordered schwean chicken with schwean fried rice and for myself i ordered mongolian mix fried rice. The quantity was good but the taste and quality was maching the price tag(mediocre). The schwean fried rice was really very spicy unlike the mongolian one. Both the quantities were enough to fill our tummies. But the quality of the rice used in the fried rice were very normal.¬†

Overall: When you are really hungry,does't bother about the quality of food,and the decors, this place promises to satisfy your wish in every sector.

2016-07-23 02:20:10
Soumyadip Banerjee/the_bigfatfoodie
27343204
3.0
Location: If you're coming from exide, this place will be on your left. Cross the lane that leads to forum, keep going straight, keep an eye for an aisle on your left. head straight down the aisle, turn right and you'll find this eatery.

Ambience: dark and shabby with red china lights hanging from the ceiling. Plastic chairs and the use of age old crockery( some of the plates have broken edges) worsen the experience .I've been here quite a few times, especially when I run low on cash. Food Quality and the overall hygine of this place is really questionable. Once you spot the open drains, the dirty kitchen and the place where they wash the dishes, you won't have the appetite for sure.However, I like their pork dishes ( the dry preparations). Momos here is good but not worth the hype. The pan fried momos have soggy coatings and Sweet and sour chicken tastes like boiled mixture of water and ketchup.¬†
If you have a stomach made of steel, give this place a visit.

##

2016-07-21 21:02:21
Oishik Sarkar
3119605
2.0
Don't know about gem but this one is truly a hidden place. Well known for their Momos but very difficult to find. Patience is virtue with this good expectation shall we start this journey?

Location : Take a deep breath before you start to search this place. Better if you like adventure. First locate the HDFC Bank on Elgin Road that is near to one of a Rabindra Sadan metro gate out. Just opposite to that you will find M/s. M. Das. Jewellers. Cross the road & just beside that you will find a very thin lane. Don't get afraid enter into that lane & go straight then take right. There's no banner or hooding outside, so its impossible in every angle to understand that there's a restaurant inside. So be prepare for that.

Decorations : It was like getting into a cave, dark ambience inside, lights focused on the tables only. There was sittings for hardly 16-20 people managed withing very small space.

Staffs & Management : At that time a single person was there to take the orders & serve the food. Even the restaurant was pretty empty at that time still they took quite a long to serve the food on table. So order whatever you need at once.

Food : With pretty obies choice we started the journey with their momos & ended up trying few items. There was quite a large options to choose from various Chinese dishes.

Pork Pan Fried Momo : As per other reviewers on Zomato their Momos are must try. These were one of the most biggest momos I had tried. Unlike other pan fried momos this one was just steamed momos dipped into the tangy sauce. Momos were big in size but it was absolutely empty inside. Only 10% was filled with the pork meat. Sauce was excessive tangy & over spicy that didn't tasted good. Personally I didn't found anything to be liked about their momos. Actually it was less momo more pickle.

Chilli Garlic Egg Hakka Noodles : Noodles were served in a plate & of very thin quality. Vegetables were very nicely sliced, eggs were fried & mixed well. But good things stopped here, garlic was diced into small pieces in it, that felt odd crunchy in mouth & got stuck in teeth. It was not how garlic noodles should be & it just made the taste worst. Although it wasn't very oily but the quantity was pretty less.

Roast Chilli Pork Dry : A restaurant can't make good pork isn't a good Chinese Restaurant for me. Roast Chilli Pork is most common over here. Served in a plate sliced pork pieces were pretty big. But diced capsicum & onion pieces were used more than the meat itself. Meat was nicely tendered, spicy & well cooked. It tasted good but not very good cause I had tried better pork than this before.

Pricing : Pricing on the menu card was quite similar to other simple Chinese restaurants. Our total bill for all the above mentioned dishes were Rs. 375 with no extra Vat or Service Tax. But considering the food's quantity, quality & non AC environment I can't say it a satisfactory one.

Conclusion : Coming to the final words, A low on pocket Chinese hub famous & highly rated for their Momos, Is It really good? Is it recommended? Well, Absolutely Not. The food quality was not up to the mark & not at all preferable for Chinese food lovers.

##

2016-07-03 20:34:06
Shreya Bhowmick
2526344
4.0
This is a hidden gem in true sense.I dropped by this place with some friends after shopping.It took us hell lot of time to find it.It's located in a narrow dingy lane.But it's worth the visit just for the sake of really good food at a pocket friendly rate.

We ordered a chicken sweet corn soup and panfried pork momos.

‚ñ∂‚ñ∂Chicken sweet corn soup-Every mouthful was a complete delight.Soup was thick,had the right balance of sweetness in it with ample amount of chicken and sweet corn.It was an ideal hearty bowl of warm soup on a rainy evening.

‚ñ∂‚ñ∂Panfried chicken momo-This was the only disappointing dish from this place.Coating was too thick,momos weren't at all crispy as expected it panfried momo and I didn't like the sauce too it was tossed in.

Mains we ordered were mixed garlic gravy noodles,mixed mongolian fried rice and roasted chilli pork.All were top notch.

‚ñ∂‚ñ∂Mongolian fried rice-We wanted to have 1 spicy staple but not as schezuan.We took this on suggestion of our server saying that this will be mildly spicy and tangy.It lived upto the description.We liked it a lot..It was a good dish

‚ñ∂‚ñ∂Mixed garlic gravy noodles-I loved this more than the rice dish..so much that i would've licked the plate if i was at home! :P
The gravy tasted so good with loads of veggies,meat and prawns.Flavour of garlic was infused in a beautiful subtle manner so that it doesn't overpower the delicate flavour..but the presence of garlic was very pronounced.Completely loved it.

‚ñ∂‚ñ∂Chilli pork(dry)-This was a winner dish.Pork was finely sliced and not at all rubbery/chewy.It was very tender but was spiced with a good kick in it.The stir fried veggies in it were good too.I love to have pork which is very spicy and Tibetan Delight exactly gave me that.

I'm surely going to drop by at this place many more times in future when I'll want to have a sumptuous pork meal without burning a hole in my pocket.

The Restaurant is inside a typical serpentine Kolkata lane.The entrance is a major turn off. It is a low budget restaurant with no sprawling space. The service is fast & they offer quality food. The dishes are lip smacking. One must try out the typical Tibetan delicacies.

Nth Visit:
I have a robust reason regarding decreasing my rating from 4 stars to 2 stars. All my previous visits to Tibetan Delight never led to sheer disappointment unlike this one. I chose to takeaway Chicken Steam Momo and Egg Thukpa. The moment I reached home and opened the packets, I found the momos were all fragmented into pieces. Is that possible? I tried gulping down a piece and found it to be outright stale & tasteless. Although the Egg Thukpa was delicious but I found a strand of hair in it. (-_- ) Terrible! I discarded it immediately. Adding to my plight, I have a upset stomach since the last night. I never expected their quality to go down the gutter. Clearly going to rethink about the further visits.

##

2016-06-30 05:43:03
Arunima
30001801
1.5
Inspiration to visit?
I have heard about this place a lot. One of my friends is a big fan of this place as it's cheap. I used to think they are really great as I heard a lot. I have visited all other restaurants around it but since it's location is weird I could never find it out! At last i became determined and decided to visit here anyway.
Location?
U will never be able to find it out if u r not accompanied by someone who knows. Honestly speaking being a girl I literally got scared while walking through that damp dark extremely narrow lane where only one can walk at a time.
Ambience?
They really tried. Some lights and 4tables are there but the place looks really shabby and unhygienic nomatter how they tried.
Food?
I have heard 'DRY CHILLY PORK' is their special dish! So is pork and chicken MOMO and their special Thupka! Ordered then all together with a plate of mixed chow mein. The only thing we could eat was the noodles!
Thupka? The soup tasted pathetic! The noodle strands had just no flavours! Not much veggies were there and the little amount present was not properly boiled.
Momo? Yes the size was big! But does size really matter that much?! I tasted better momos from the hawkers! Momos tasted so dull! Not much chicken or pork filling was there! Only onions n onions! The covering had no such taste. Too much dull.
The most important one! Their special Dry chili pork??
The most disgusting, pathetic and worst pork dish I have ever had! The meat was inedible! So damn hard! Chewing a rubber could have been much easier! No flavours, not at all juicy! No sign of any pork fat! Nothing absolutely!! We complained, they said they will change the dish! Change? They brought back the same pieces of rubbery meat after heating them! We were completely shocked! They complained again! It was inedible!!! We asked them to change the dish! Those pathetic pieces of inedible meat!! They just didn't want to do that! Though they admitted that their meat was faulty yet they didn't! They told us that their was an issue with their meat shop so the pork was not good for that day! If they could accept that then why couldn't they just change it??
Finally after a lot of disgust we came out throwing away all those nasty food right there! They dismissed the pork dish at last. We paid fr the rest.
Pathetic service! Disgusting experience!
And ladies never try to visit their washroom no matter how bad u need to go! They told me that they have one but it was horrible. No lights, no water, no lock.

##

2016-06-16 03:00:16
Panchali Kar
31717365
4.5
Tibetan delight is not just an eatery, it's sheer nostalgia. If you haven't eaten Chinese and Tibetan food in one of these dingy, oldish restaurants, you must have been missing something. Being situated in a narrow, dark lane and being clumsy and wretched in decor, it may appear unappealing to certain eaters however that exactly is the charm of this place. And mind you, this place is NOT unhygienic. Go only if you don't have tantrums regarding apparent cleanliness and decor.

Pork is the signature attraction, though fish, chicken and prawn dishes are equally good. For me smoked or roasted chilli pork is a must. Then comes the other items like the momos, or noodles, or chopusey. The noodles are indeed worth a try.

If you are comfortable with eating in shady places this place is worth a try. You won't be disappointed.

2016-06-16 03:00:16
Panchali Kar

4.5
Tibetan delight is not just an eatery, it's sheer nostalgia. If you haven't eaten Chinese and Tibetan food in one of these dingy, oldish restaurants, you must have been missing something. Being situated in a narrow, dark lane and being clumsy and wretched in decor, it may appear unappealing to certain eaters however that exactly is the charm of this place. And mind you, this place is NOT unhygienic. Go only if you don't have tantrums regarding apparent cleanliness and decor.

Pork is the signature attraction, though fish, chicken and prawn dishes are equally good. For me smoked or roasted chilli pork is a must. Then comes the other items like the momos, or noodles, or chopusey. The noodles are indeed worth a try.

If you are comfortable with eating in shady places this place is worth a try. You won't be disappointed.

2016-06-06 12:45:08
Sumit Surai
11641
3.5
Tibetan Delight for me is more than a restaurant. It is nostalgia. I started going to this place when a plate of steamed pork momos was just rupees 16. This place used to be our savior when we were hungry after a movie or adda at Nandan and couldn't afford expensive places. Prices have shot up, but it is still pocket friendly.

A place cannot run for so long just for being pocket friendly. The food here is good too. Yes, they are a bit inconsistent, but most of the time you will be satisfied with the food here. 

It is located in a narrow lane behind the other Tibetan restaurants of the locality, so a bit tough to locate for first timers. The single dining room might look shabby, but the dimly lit room has a mysterious ambiance of its own. 

The thukpa here is decent and filling. Momos are good. Pan fried momos, with the spicy sauce, are good options during winters. Most of the Chinese items are good. We prefer the Pork items here.

Service is really fast. During evenings, most of the times, you will have to wait to get a table. But as they are real fast they manage it well. 

In all a decent place to visit if you are around and craving some pocket friendly but good Tibetan and Chinese.

3.5
This is a good Tibetan joint in Kolkata, probably the only "nearly" authentic one, aside from Blue Poppy. Kolkata need a few like these, which serve good Tibetan pork (which is when I really miss Delhi).¬†

Location is tricky, as mentioned in the previous reviews. ¬†And I'm even worse when it comes to describing locations. So apologies for that.

Food was a 3.5 on 5 for me. We ordered:

Pork Steamed momos- Juicy with a respectable amount of stuffing. Served hot and the meat seemed fresh, what with the right smell.

Pork kothey- Pan fried momos, with stuffing that tasted very grounded and granulated and great!! Right amount of frying. Very appealing.

Pork fried rice- Honestly, didn't quite enjoy this much. I felt it was a bit more fried than usual as was evident from the grains.¬†

Pork with oyster sauce- Looked great, tasted even better, good portions of fresh meat and right portions of fat and flesh.¬†

Will definitely visit the place once again to try the other pork delicacies as I am a big fan of Tibetan pork dishes. Good place to eat.

##

2016-04-06 17:47:44
Sohom Paul
2263166
4.5
Tibetan Delight is the kind of place you'd hear of from a friend, who heard it from this friend, who once visited the place and found it to be great.

And this is absolutely right!

Located in a little dingy alleyway between sullen buildings, the place is hard to spot for the uninitiated. Take that friend along, or ask the locals. Just a few minutes of exploration away from Exide Metro station, this little house is tucked away in semi darkness: the kind of place you'd expect seedy people to gather around tables and discuss all kinds of mischief.

Walk in. Make yourself at home. All the people there (oh, there always ARE people there) won't appear as seedy in the dim red lantern light. The food will always be warm, abundant, and delicious. The lady at the counter, or the cook behind the window are always hospitable, and are a fountain of stories.

The ambiance is warm, not just because it is enjoyable, but also because there is no AC. Gather around your table with three other friends, and relish your meal. The taste and affordability of the food will make you re-visit again and again.
 The simple decor will stay with you, and make the search for the place worth it.

It's the kind of place you'd tell a friend about, and expect them to tell another friend of theirs.

2016-04-02 21:19:45
Chatterjee SM(Chatujjebabu)
2135434
4.0
Well, that's what is called a hidden gem in the heart of Kolkata- Yes, "Tibetan Delight" surely deserve this tagline. Located at a dingy narrow lane, parallel to Suburban Hospital Road, this restaurant apparently appears to be a bit shabby.  The interior space is pretty small and congested, with around 4 tables(with 4 chairs in each table). And you may have to wait for a table if the tables are already filled with guests. Oh, yeah!! Its a non AC place.
But the decor inside resembles an old school Tibetan charm, and once you take the first bite, the show begins with the delicious treat to pamper your taste buds. Genuinely authentic and mouth watering delights is the ultimate USP of this place, which is sure to make your day. Trust me, you'll forget all the cons I mentioned in the first paragraph, after having the food. Yes, the taste is more than enough to compensate all the cons, and ultimately you'll come back with a smiling face.
A must visit for all the foodies out there.

Note- The pork and prawn pieces in Thukpa will have a signature generic smell. That does not mean it is unfit for consumption. If you don't like the smell, you may avoid Thukpa and try out the other options.

2015-12-19 17:44:49
Petuk Baba
790102
3.0
Well this place had been on my wishlist for a long period of time due to its hype from foodies all around kolkata. So i decided to visit this place today with my friends for a delightful lunch.

Well the first thing was to find this hidden place which was tricky indeed. To locate this you have to take the narrow lane opposite of hdfc bank. Just keep going inside & you will see their board hanging there. The place is shabby. Upon reaching there we found a long queue waiting for their turn. So approximately we had to wait for 45mins until we were seated by the helper over there. After being seated we quickly ordered the following:-

1. Pan fried chicken lollipop- 8 pieces of chicken lollis served in spicy chilli & tomato sauce with sauted onion,lemongrass & capsicum. The taste was splendid & the lollis were succulent but the chilli factor was on the higher which gave a great taste to our buds. Recommended & do specify to the helper to make it milder if you cant bear the chilli factor.

2. Veg schezwan friedrice- This dish was very disappointing due to the fact that the rice was undercooked which made the dish bland.

3. Chilli garlic veg chow- This was very tasty & the spice factor was good in but my complain would be the high amount of oil being used to prepare the dish. Overall I was left dissatisfied.

4. Hot garlic chicken- Our original order was chicken in thai sauce but it was unavailable & so we went for this item. 9 pieces of succulent chicken were served in garlic sauce along with onions. The spice factor was ok.

The quantity of chow is well on the higher side as compared to the rice. Overall my experience was okayish. The pocket pinch was on the lower side since our bill came to rs.630 for 3 people. They could improve more!!

2015-12-15 15:18:12

4.5
Writing the review for one particular momo place reminded me of Tibetan Delight. And I felt a sharp pang of guilt for not having written a review for my most favourite momo place in the whole city. Yes the food is fantastic, but it's got a lot to do with nostalgia for me as well. I have had some of the best moments here with my partner and it's one of the places which we have made "our special little place", right since the time I was a poor little college student with not much money to spend.¬†

Tucked away in a dingy little gulley, it's pretty hard to find, but that's what adds to its charm as well. A tiny little place, there have been many times when we have had to patiently wait for one of the tables to clear. The decor is frugal, with red Chinese lanterns and around 4 tables to seat people. If you are visiting, have no pretentions of a fine dining experience. Value for money, delectable Tibetan food? Yes, that's something you will definitely find.
Coming to the food, it's one of the best place for momos without a shadow of a doubt. The steamed chicken momos are succulent and wonderfully fresh every time we had tried it. Never let us down. The pan fried chicken momos are heady and spicy and we usually order it with a plate of chicken fried rice. Generous portions and pairs wonderfully well. We love it! 2 plates of steam chicken momos, a side of pan fried momos and fried rice, washed down with Thums Up is our staple menu over here and we have never really ventured beyond it. Oh yes, the kotheys are brilliant too! The second best I have had, really.¬†I think we did try the garlic chicken and the stir fried noodles one one occasion, but the momos are the main reason we visit Tibetan Delight. That, and a whole lot of memories.

2015-11-27 00:19:53
Manish Gulati
530469
4.5
Locating this place reminded of those famous chase scenes of the underworld movies, running through tight lanes, turning at sharp angles, passing the staring windows, jumping over buckets of soap filled water; only the chase in this case leads to a queue of hungry souls waiting outside, to get a table :) The Yautchas and the Mainland china give you the inferior versions of these momos and you pay through your nose eating those dumplings made of cardboard compared to these puppies here. If you get a table here after 7pm, do visit your place of worship next day to thank your stars.

Inside lie just four red tables, all lit by deep red lanterns to make you feel as if you have entered the dragon's lair. The dragon himself sits at the end of the room staring at his world with his sharp squinting eyes. We ordered steamed pork momos and panfried pork momos in schezwan sauce. Both came with a bowl of warm broth. Now, how can one make a better momo than another? the key lies in the filling, the thinness of the dough wrap and the artful skill of those pretty little curly folds making each momo look like a piece of art. While the steamed pork was oozing with umami, the pan fried version like a naughty twin of the sombre brother, teased all our senses with its sweet and spicy rich coating.

After all that yummy pork, my mind craved for some more and I ordered smoked pork with red pepper. This is what I would describe as a perfect aftersex food, or even a mind starter if you are leading a dull boring life cuz it shakes ur senses from inside and you view your mind as an outsider questioning your entire belief system :)

Good foods do that, they are orgasmic and they stir your soul. Good food is like a guru that makes you get rid of all the pretensions and you eat, making your hands dirty, with your face smeared in all those yummy sauces :)

To be very clear--¬†
For Food; A big thumbs Up and 5 out of 5¬†
For hygiene, location and overall atmosphere- Thumbs Down, only 1 Out of 5¬†

Tibetan Delight, the most talked about eatery for serving mouth watering Momos and other Chinese & Tibetan delicacies, really live up to its expectation when it comes to their food. I tried their Thupkas, Chicken Kothey and Chilly Peeper Chicken. All the dishes are tasty and indulge your taste bud to urge for more. The quantity is decent enough. Price is reasonable, as the place is without A.C & providing manual bills.¬†

Its located in a dingy lane of Elgin Road and most importantly, the immediate entrance and waiting area is inhospitable, untidy with open drains. One cant avoid to close his eyes to this "Spectacle", as one need to compulsorily wait outside, as the joint can hardly accommodate 10 people at a time. ¬†Its a painful experience to witness such a pathetic ambiance in such a celebrated food joint. Though the inner part of this small eatery is marginally better and the services is quiet prompt and timely.¬†
Through this forum I would like to personally request the TD Authorities to take care of the basic hygiene & ambiance of this place. ¬†
Thank You.

2015-08-14 00:11:47
Srija Moulik
3119378
4.0
I have been going to this place then n now from my college days and this place is just still the same. This place serves the best momo in town,hands down!! The location of this place is quite tricky...and its actually quite difficult to find the place for the first time as it is in one of the shabby dark lanes at elgin road. But with a little effort put right for the location, this culinary experience in this place is worth every bit of it. This place has nothing mentionworthy about exterior decor or sitting area with a maximum sitting of 20. But tibetian delight is all about great food. I have been here many times and tried out many things but my favourites are definitely the steamed momos, the pan fried ones, and their thukpa. The momos here are soft with a thin coat and ample amount of chicken inside. The thukpa and the other soups are quite tasty but  their signature dish would definitely be  the roast chilli pork dry. It is the most delicious dish that I have ever had and absolutely nothing comes even close to it. The pork is well cooked and the chilli and onions sauted  along with it  gives a delightful flavour to the taste buds. Its a must order dish from my side whenever i visit this place. The price of the food items is fair with the quality. Hence if you are a true foodie at heart and can cope up a little with the shabby environment this place is undoubtedly a food paradise.

2015-07-06 12:03:23
Sudipta Sarkar
1043815
4.0
Tibetian Delight is a very small joint located in a congested lane near  Rabindrasadan metro station. Though a bit difficult to locate the place for first timers, we found it quickly since a friend took us there a year ago for a takeaway. I went there yesterday with my beau to have some good Chinese delicacies for lunch. We went around 2pm and found the joint quite empty with just 4 people having lunch. Since we heard a lot about this place being famous for momos I wanted to try chicken pan fried momo. But my beau insisted on chilly pepper chicken as the starter so I went for it. It tasted awesome. The chicken was saute with bell peppers, garlic and sauces and garnished with coriander leaves. It had a peppery taste, but not the burnt pepper one but the one that soothed your taste buds. Next we had veg Hakka noodles, veg fried rice and schezwan chicken. The rice tasted moderate but the chicken and noodles tasted quite good. Moreover the quantity of the food served was more than enough for us. And it was a 'Voila!' moment when the bill came. Rupees 430 only with no other service charges! A must-visit for everyone if you want a hearty meal without a pinch in your pocket.

You go to Tibetan Delight when you:

(A)
1. Are dying for some Chinese, Tibetan unconventional dishes
2. Don't give a damn about the location and ambiance
3. Don't mind walking down creepy lanes to reach your destination
4. Want to do something crazy suddenly
5. Take a creepy selfie somewhere and eat happily too

1. Decor: Don't bother. Just focus on the food.
2. Staffs: Just one guy. He serves the food on time. Be happy.
3. Food: Lovely.
4. Complimentary Drinks: Nya.6. Crowd: Decent
7. Value for money: Depends on your definition of value.8. Referable: Yes
9. Alcohol: No

Good place for first date: If she is unconventional, she'll love it.

Positive Points: Food, ambiance¬†
Negative Points: There could be many, but just don't bother.

2015-06-06 20:05:51
Abhishek Das
64692
4.5
If you live to eat, and can go any miles to have the best dishes then this place is for you.
Secretly hidden in a narrow ally on the opposite foot of the HDFC bank Bhwanipur branch the place is small with just four tables and does not provide the comfort of air condition. For some the place may consider the place shady and dirty. But all this complaints will surely vanish once you take a bite on their delicious dishes.

This place was in my wishlist for quite a long time. Even though finding the place was bit difficult but the taste of the food compensated the struggle.

Coming to the food, we ordered mixed fried rice, mixed thupka, and chilli chicken. The fried rice was awesome with tons of chicken and pork and prawns and egg. Chilli chicken had a very different taste from what I had earlier in other places, and it was different in a good sense it came with 8 pieces of succulent boneless chicken and chunks of bell papers and onions. Last but not the least the mighty mixed thukpa. A bowl full of happiness with noodles, meat, prawns cooked in chicken stock.
On the table you can grab the various sauces, chilli viniger, and dark soya sauce. Mix them to you dishes in right ratio and experience the magical flavour in your mouth. The quantity of food per dish is huge, can be share by two people easily. In fact me and my girlfriend had to pack the thukpa cos we were so full eating the mixed fried rice and chilli chicken.

It's worth a second visit. Only thing I would suggest to the owners is that they should put a sign board outside the ally and just clean the place a bit more. Lightning should be improved a bit. Looking forward to the next visit.

On the second visit,
We ordered pan fried chicken momo and chicken thukpa. The sauce of the pan fried momo was awesome and the momos were tasty too. However the stuffing could have been more. The chicken thukpa was outstanding. Previously I tried their mixed thukpa and this time chicken thukpa and I must say both tasted differently awesome.
A must visit place you are a Chinese food lover.

2015-05-18 19:58:41
Nabanita Sarkar
29240180
4.5
Tucked away inside a dingy alley is this small restaurant delighting the foodies with its delicious momos, sumptuous pork pan fries, and warm comforting thupkas. Although a bit difficult to locate (right opposite Rabindra Sadan metro's gate no 4) and a bit small, the piping hot food served on a budget makes up for it.

Try their speciality, the spicy hot pan fried pork momos (fair warning: it's very hot). And if you have a more delicate palate try their steamed momos which comes with a mixed broth. Do try their thupkas which always reminds me of Darjeeling. For side dish try their Fried pork with BBQ sauce or Fried pork with oyster sauce, both of which are a steal at the price they serve.

If you're more into Chinese, they serve some spicy rice dishes here, my favourite being the fried rice. They also do a mean Garlic chicken and fairly good Manchurian chicken to go with that.

The food is served quick and never in all my years had it ever been less than perfect.
Don't miss this one.

How could I have not been to Tibetan Delight earlier? Well nevertheless, sooner or later, for the sheer love of food, do drop by. Having heard oodles about this restaurant from innumerous people, I finally reached Tibetan Delight, positioned at the end of what I‚Äôd call a maze.

If you finally happen to find your way out right, you‚Äôll walk into a small restaurant enveloped in blue with dimly lit red and yellow lights. With accommodation for only a handful, and a table for 4, very informally placed on the outside, colossal patience or vast luck is required to get you a table here. This place is always crammed with people and chattering noises lingering around the restaurant. 

Determined, we waited for almost 40 minutes after which we finally got seated, hunger struck. The menu slopes more to the Chinese side, and everyone unanimously agreed that they served some of the most delectable pork in town. We ordered a portion of Mongolian rice followed by one of Roast Chilli Pork, as suggested by a friend. Firstly I need to mention, they are anything but frugal when it comes to their quantity they dole out. The Mongolian rice tasted liked ordinary fried rice, nonetheless pleasant. What absolutely blew my mind was that pork. It is beautifully roasted, cooked to aptness, not chewy and yet not buttery tender. It‚Äôs more about savoring the pork because it awakens all your possible taste buds.

Their momos is what they are known for. But after gorging on endless helpings of pork, I decided to leave some surprise for the next visit, because how can you not come back to a place like this. Surprisingly, so much so, without even burning a large hole in your pockets. Each dish is priced reasonably maximizing your satiety while keeping your wallets happy. However, I‚Äôd like to mention of course, this place might not be aesthetically pleasing, in fact is not one bit, it is clumsily located but I guarantee that if you‚Äôre able to get past that mind block, you are in for an exultant indulgence. Until next time‚Ä¶

Can‚Äôt wait to go back! :)

##

2014-12-16 22:08:10
Rupsa Das
650008
4.0
Take a bit of dirty and shabby entrance and add it up with delicious food, you get Tibetian delight. Definitely, this is a place that lives upto its name. Delightful. If you start thinking from a broad aspect, this small, cramped up room would appear mysteriously romantic to you! I have eaten here before too but let's review about it.

I have a bad affinity towards pork and this is not something that would easily disappear. And Tibetian Delight is known to serve awesome pork. So, me and my partner S, decided to land up here and have some awesome pork. To start with the whole journey, I would have never figured out the place if it was not for S. I never figure it out! The cramped, antique lane invited us and as usual, it was crowded with people. Four tables are definitely not enough to quench the hunger of so many fans. We waited for more than half and hour before we got a table.

We both were hungry like mad and straight jumped onto the big menu. We ordered chicken fried rice, roast chili pork(semi-gravy) and chicken steamed momo. This place has an attached kitchen with all the food aromas and steam coming into the eating place and soon enough turns the place into a sneeze-fest. I was a prey to this fest too with endless sneeze and coughs. However, the food arrived soon after and I was too hungry to care about anything else.

The quantity was moderate. A plate shared would leave you hungry for a bit more. The chicken fried rice was tasty, very similar to the taste that you would expect from the Tibetian restaurants. However, the chicken that they give with it, is very dry. It's so dry that if you chew on it, it would seem like dry paper. However, the chili pork is delectable. They give you a 3/4th filled bowl of the dish and it smells amazing. The bowl is loaded with pork and definitely it quenched my pork thirst for sometime. I had loads of pork with the gravy which is packed with garlic. However, the capsicum, that should be present in a chili gravy was missing. It had very less capsicum.
After finishing the main meal, it left both me and S hungry for more. So we ordered chicken steamed momo. The steam momo arrived soon after and it was big. The size of the momo is big but it is not exactly juicy and succulent. It is an above average tasting momo with a soup that actually is clear and tastes only like chicken stock.¬†
Oh and finished it off with a thumps up!

Positives: The food, the service and the authenticity. The best part is the price.¬†

Negatives: The cramped up space, the wait.¬†

Th bill rounded up to around 300/-, which is affordable like anything as nowadays, a small lipstick costs you much, much more than that. A hearty meal with such awesome contentment, surely costs more.

I have visited this place more than once and I would definitely visit this place again!

4.0
The Tibetan Delight - what can be written about this delightful place, excepting that it is an absolute delight to visit it every time. We, implying my husband and I have been visiting this place from the time we were in college and we still do so even after a decade. The food is something that you can never forget, the experience being one of the most exhilarating for your taste buds. The simple Thai and Chinese dishes are kept so - simple and that is were the actual delight of the place is. My all time favourite is the mixed thukpa. Closely to follow is the roasted chilli pork. One of the best joint for pork lovers. The pork is left juicy and succulent and not over cooked like most other joints around. My husband's all time favourite is their mixed fried rice with any of the pork dishes, mostly of the roasted variety. The momos are delicious ... almost yummy to the taste of infinity. 
The only drawback being the location that is hard to find without proper signage and the rather too less number of seats. But then I think that is the main essence of the place, it is never to be found empty. That is the amount of popularity it had amongst the Kolkatans.

2014-07-22 11:41:50
Ankur Banik
737186
4.0
Tibetan Delight is a long time personal favourite of mine and one may say I am a bit biassed towards this place.But the fact of the matter is that Tibetan Delight has been delighting me for a long long time.
It is a bit difficult to locate at first.You will find this place once you enter a narrow shabby alley while proceeding from Elgin road towards the Chai break fifth element.The first time I visited I was kinda fascinated by the shabby entrance which suddenly led to a Darjeeling-esque small cosy dimly lit place filled with wonderful aroma.In fact after innumerable visits I still am fascinated! The place is small with four tables accommodating around 15 people and there is no air conditioning.
In spite of the presence of Momo plaza,Hamro momo,Orchid etc which are similar places are more renowned places for most people located in the vicinity Tibetan Delight has always been my preferred place among all these.
The menu is quite diverse offering various Chinese and Tibetan dishes.The momos are wonderfully soft.The pan fried momos are one of the best you will have albeit a little too spicy for my liking at times.They make a wonderful kothey.This was the place where I had kotheys for the first time and I have been a big fan of them ever since.The soup and thukpa are also very nice and perfect during the winter months.I make it a point to visit every winter for the thukpa,momos,kotheys and the spicy pan fried momos.The main course is also pretty tasty and the quantities are quite generous.The pork items here are very good and one of my personal picks is the roasted chili pork.
The serive is swift.The prices are very reasonable and they do not charge any vat or service tax.The prices have gone up a bit over the years and honestly the quality has also become a wee bit inconsistent of late.This is the reason for me deducting 0.5 from my rating.But still this remains one of those places which are close to my heart.

Location: Bhawanipore.

This little eatery is tucked away in an alley adjacent to M. Das Jewellers.
It can be reached by keeping to your left while moving towards P.C. Chandra from Exide, after you cross Chai Break (Elgin).
Once in the alley, the aroma of the food which surrounds the air, would easily lead you till the joint. ;)
There isn't any ambiance as such. Had a small seating capacity with just four tables (Sixteen heads at one go). One thing to add to it's plus is that they have placed a couple of benches outside the restaurant for the people waiting to be seated (Yes, it's pretty crowded thanks to its quality of fooding).
The lanterns hanging just above your table looks nice, but, you might just bang your head while eating since it's quite low. :-P
You might spot rats running across the lane you walk through. :-P

Had been near bhawanipore along with a few colleagues for some work and were famished when this place crossed my mind. And, here we were for a quick bite which later turned into a heavy meal owing to the delicious dishes which made us order more. :P
Hands-down authentic preparation it was!

Our order comprised of the following:

Steamed Momos (Veg)
The steamed momos were perfectly steamed, the wrap wasn't thick and had a flavorful and generous stuffing comprising of shredded carrots and cabbage. (Five pieces a plate).
Tasted great.
-Sadly, no clear soup was served along.

Pan-fried Momos (Veg)
The steamed momos were pan-tossed in a mildly-spiced yet, amazingly flavorful Sichuan sauce with saut√©d garlic and spring onions. (Five pieces per plate)
Delicious.
Recommended.

Schezwan Rice
This was ordered on the recommendation of the server there.
And, we didn't mind ordering since we all over already head over heels on their Sichuan sauce preparation.
Undoubtedly, this dish tasted great!
Recommended.

The server was friendly and prompt in processing our order.
The service was brisk.

A pocket friendly affair.

Overall a good experience.
-Highly recommended for people who wouldn't mind the ambiance. And, others who wish to try the delicious offerings should also give it a try. :)

##

2014-07-01 04:44:24
Ananyak 'Kash' Saha
495119
4.0
A small little joint located in a tiny lane beside Rabindra Sadan metro station, this has become a hub for youngsters in a short amount of time. The first thing that'll strike you as a downside is the location, although located in a prime position, it is situated in a shabby little lane that many may deem unsafe and many would prefer to avoid the place solely coz of the location. It's dingy and I cannot really guarantee the hygiene but what I can guarantee is the taste of the food.
As a college goer,  I always look for places that serves tasty food without draining my pocket and this was an amazing find. Reasonably priced, and tasty food is always a good thing.
The pan fried pork momos are amazing, even the steamed momos are a marvel. I prefer pork momo over chicken but they make both pretty good here. Chicken in Barbecue Sauce and Roast Chili Pork were much better than I had expected. Pork Chop Suey was very tasty but the Thai Chop Suey was a let down as there was no material, no pork chicken or anything. They might have served veg for some reason even after repeating the order a few times. Pork with Schezwan Sauce was also good, and manchurian chicken was standard.
Now do not get carried away, when I say that the food is amazing, you must always keep in mind the price you are paying, compared to that it is amazing, it would be an injustice to compare it to well known expensive restaurants. But as for me the price plays an important factor, in my opinion this is good place to hog.
I do have complaints against the staff as there is only one man taking the order and he's very slow to respond and it seems as if he is in his own world. Although the food doesn't take very long to arrive. And it'd be good if the place was air conditioned but that might be a bit too much to ask.
A must visit to all college goers and momo lovers. The place is mainly famous for it's pork momo which you should definitely try.

‚ÄúYou don‚Äôt need a silver fork to eat Good food‚Äù ‚Äì that‚Äôs all about Tibetan Delight. The very first day when I visited this restaurant, the first thing came into my mind was ‚Äúhow dirty‚Äù. Coming to the food section, starting with the momos, this is what Tibetan Delight is really famous for. It provides you delicious momos (both steam and fried). 2014-06-01 21:48:55
Shakri Banerjee

3.5
From today this is the go to place for me when I crave good chilli pork!!
This place has been there for ages and I have been visiting since my college days. Rock bottom prices seemed heavenly for our restricted budget. One of the best momo I have had and the place where I discovered the delights of the Thupka!!
But in recent years I have not really been here. But today on a whim and under the whim of this uncontrollable craving for chilli pork I decided to hit T D since I was in that area. And boy was I surprised!! I had expected a chilli pork with generously loaded with pork fat but instead found amazingly lean portion (just one piece containing fat!!). The dish was not overly spicy like some other places and was quite balanced!!
Yes its dirty and hard to find but then I recommend the people complaining so to steer clear since seems to me that they have been lucky enough to have experianced lavish stetile places but unfortunate enough not to have split 2 happy plates of momo between 3 people and still happy to have jst enough money for the bus home.
This place is what it is. Period.

2014-05-12 21:39:11
Kingshuk Bhattacharya
155296
2.5
What did all, yes, all of my friends saw in TD that I didn't? No, I mean, seriously, so below average a place has such word of mouth! Only because it is easy on the pockets? Maybe.

The location: For the first timers, don't forget to take someone with you who's been there before, or be prepared to ask plenty of people for the direction plenty of times. Situated in a shady and possibly one of Kolkata's narrowest by-lanes, you have to cross a couple of drains on the way, and after that, you have two choices. Either you're fired up and super hungry, or if you're like me, all of your previous excitement is out of the window. The interior is fine, small place, four tables, Chinese lanterns  hanging from the ceiling, giving the room a warm red glow. No problem.

We ordered Steamed Pork Momos and Mixed Chinese Chopsuey and had planned on ordering a thukpa later. The momos arrived almost instantly. How? It was brought out of the refrigerator, heated and served. The skin was thick, chewy, so much that we dumped it and ate the filing with the broth and the sauce, not spicy enough to accompany momos IMO. Pissed, we completely focused on the Chopsuey at hand, only to find out after the first spoonful that it was too sweet for our liking. The amount was generous enough, but we couldn't finish even 3/4th of it and ditched the idea to order thukpa. 

Definitely not impressed. Might give it another try to see if it was a bad day in the kitchen. Till then, I'll trust the Sami Roll from Saima to save us like it did this day.

2014-05-05 22:31:55
Tarun
1155456
3.5
Great reviews, decide to visit the place, hard to find, shabby surroundings, small tiny restaurant, long waiting time, disappointed, get a table, just want to eat n go n never return, food comes, amazing food, love the food, decide to try its other items again, may be would prefer it for a takeaway next time ..............thats Tibetan Delight in short.............

Located in a small alley bye-lane exactly opposite PC Chandra, the place might be a bit harder to find than one is prepared after having already read about it in almost all the other reviews. Its a small restaurant with just 4 tables in a small room. And thanks to the great n consistent food it serves, there is always some queue which becomes even more troublesome since the waiting space is pretty dirty n stinky. The place is small, packed, very dimly lit and no air conditioning. The service is pretty fast.
¬†
Coming to food, the food is pretty good with extremely reasonable prices and generous serving. The steamed momos are really good and one of the most sasta in the whole city. The red pepper sauce is pretty average alongside. The noddles are well made and tasty. Obviously the quality of noodles isnt top notch but pretty well made to be liked. The vegetables are decent but few of them are pretty nice especially the garlic veg, babycorn manchurian. Szechwan fried rice is well made and could be tried if one is of with spiced up food.

Overall, the food is really value for money but i would prefer orchid restaurant nearby which serves better food in more decent sitting arrangements but charges a 20-30 percent premium and as far as tibetan delights is concerned, it would be my recommendation to go for a takeaway rather than eating inside

2014-05-04 08:11:48
Samit Roychoudhury
349869
3.0
This tiny joint, perhaps the original one of the ones dotting Suburban Hospital Road has been there for as long as I care to remember. I remember the first few visits we had trouble finding the place. One would enter through a narrow alley on the main road, walk quite a few feet and take a right and suddenly land up in the courtyard of a house. That was it. Tibetan Delight. For many it was the last word in Momos.

Four tables meant long queues. The dark alley meant stepping out into almost unknown territory when you finished. But yet the crowds kept coming, into this not too clean, not too efficient place to have Momos. And what momos. They were decent, but the broth had a chaat masala like taste to it that would always put me off. Meat masala I presume. Portions and pricing was decent of course. I never really tried anything else. Looking at the present menu, I see it is still may less expensive than other places.

Must visit again soon.

2014-04-21 00:46:27
Kanchan Yadav
777965
4.0
Absolute gem of a place if you're into pork. Was introduced to this place by a friend, and it took quite an effort to find out the place. The first look of the place was enough to make us think about turning back, but we are so glad that we did not. There is seating arrangement for about 15 people and in busy days you have to wait a while to be seated. The main intention of us was to savor huge amounts of pork, and so we started with the pork steamed momo. Sadly, the fried or pan fried ones were not available. They tasted alright, not anything outstanding. Then for the main course we ordered chilli garlic noodles, roasted chilli pork, and sliced pork in hot garlic sauce. The noodles did not have any garlicky flavor whatsoever, but tasted good. However, the food of the day were the pork items. The roasted chilli pork was just the right amount of chilly with a crunchy taste. The sliced pork in hot garlic was soft and succulent and almost melted in your mouth. We were 8 people, and we all eat a lot. After a very filling meal, we each ordered a bottle of soft drink, and was pleasantly surprised when the bill came to a low amount of 1400. Don't be deceived by the look of the place, it is a must try.

2014-03-17 16:41:02
Kamalika Mukherjee
178472
2.0
Everyone's been chanting hymns of Tibetan Delight but I , on the other hand find it very average.

Read on...

J coaxed me to try this eatery one fine day after a shopping session at Forum. Initially I was not very sure but then again I agreed. I had to wait outside for my turn. This is shabby little place nestled in a lane. Tough to locate for first timers.
J had been telling about how great food they serve so I ignored the ambience and the not so well made tables, chairs.
Its shanty, and has mosquitos hovering outside while one is waiting. No proper lights either. Very dimly lit place.

We were starving so without further ado, ordered Schezwan noodles and Manchurian chicken.
What came to my table left me aghast!

Thin glass noodles, with no proper seasoning or any hint of hotness in it, just the plain roadside stalls that sells noodles, a ditto version of it sat upright!
The biggest shock came when I found out that instead of serving manchurian chicken, they gave me garlic chicken. The entire dish was smelling of garlic and I kept cursing myself for giving this a try. I very well knew that this was a very popular joint but what I did not know was the standards that went down so drastically!

Disappointed and wont be back again!

2014-03-04 15:47:55
Vikramjit Dutta
965332
4.5
I have been a regular patron to this eatery from my taj days. Was introduced to this gem of a place by my first colleagues. 

Most aren't aware of this place and end up at the 3 other momo joints, on the main road, opposite rabindra sadan metro station. 

This place is hidden and one needs to venture thru one of the narrow dark lanes, between 2 old buildings. The place being so downtrodden yet always has a waiting. They have placed a small bench outside for that. Please do not look into their kitchen while waiting. It might ruin your appetiite!

The restaurant is one dimly lit small room with 5 tables - max 20 covers. 

But the food is mouth watering. The steamed momos, roast chilli pork, mixed fried rice are my favourites. 

Very easy on the pocket. Popular with students & young proffesionals.

2014-01-21 23:29:05
Trinakusum Das
1592014
4.0
I 1st heard of this place when I was in class 10 when my friends used to go out and eat here. So ever since I started studying MBBS at IPGME&R and SSKM Hospital, I have been meaning to visit this place but didnt know exactly where it was! I recently located it using zomato and finally decided to visit it today! But it seems locating it on a map wasn't quite enough as I had to ask quite a few people to understand exactly which alley it was located in. Finally having gone down the small alley I found the place and though it is a very small food joint, I quite liked the ambience of this place, specially the lantern style lamps lit over each of the table. I ordered for pork pan fried momo (deep fried), pork kothey and chicken thukpa. Service was well enough. The momo was a total treat! From the covering of the momo, to the minced meat inside and the spicy gravy in which it is tossed, everything about it was delicious! Its a real shame that they dont provide soup with the pan fried variety though. The kothey was quite tasty too. As for the thukpa, having not tried thukpa ever before I can't really judge it but if thukpa usually tastes like that, I don't think its really my cup of tea. So all in all a place of nice ambience with good food at really low cost. The location could have been better though. So I'll be rating it 4.

This place is a must for adventurous foodies !

2013-10-12 18:26:15

Our group of 7 marched into this to loot our dear friend on his Birthday treat! If you don't know this place from previously then it is a real pain to locate it the first time (even the GPS failed us)! It is located at the end of the thinnest of lanes between two houses and behind an apartment and diagnostic centre. There is an inconspicuous little yellow board announcing the place to the world.
The place is dirty to say the least! There are open drains, dogs around the very filthy and sooty kitchen and so on. The restaurant is very dark with lantern like lights covered with crimson cloth hanging from the top. Only 4 tables of 4 are available so it is not likely that you will get to seat immediately. My opinion? Try the takeaway!
We ordered smoked pork with red pepper, pork with barbecue sauce, pork with thai sauce, fish in chilli garlic sauce, hunan chicken and mixed gravy chowmein ( no prawn was available and I was surprised to find no mein foon on the menu).
The pork items were really spicy and tasty just the way I like it but the pork meat hardly had fat with it, I was very displeased with that as without fat pork tastes like chicken's poor cousin! The fish was very bad, tasted very bland and powdery. But the hunan chicken was heavenly! THe mixed chowmein was good too.
The service is slow and inefficient. The quantities of food served are decent and the prices friendly.
In short, a place for decent food for takeaways but does not justify the rating that it enjoys on zomato.

##

2013-08-17 23:53:10
Mukulita Ganguly
207896
4.0
Tibetan Delight is one of those eateries which may not boast of a high end dining experience but does enough justice to the regional cuisine and promises a pleasant gastronomic journey nonetheless.

A long narrow alley bounded by high walls off the busy Chowringhee road, with yellow sign boards flashing the name "Tibetan Delight" proudly, secretly leads to a small bend that opens up to the hidden treasure of true culinary delight.
After a lot of planning and braving the brutal sunshine on a hot summer afternoon, when we finally reached this place, it was completely full. We had to wait for a minute outside, before we were called in politely by a server. On entering, we were greeted by a tiny dark room, dimly lit up with swinging red lanterns, the unclean walls beautified with some Tibetan paintings and four tables set up at the four cozy corners, where mostly young people had gathered for lunch. My very first visit to this place brought back fond memories of the amazing little food joints and pubs in Sikkim.

Our order comprised of Pork Steamed Momo, Pork Hakka Chowmein, Roast Chilli Pork and Pork with Barbeque Sauce (yes, we were fiercely longing for a lot of pork!). The food arrived within 5 minutes and I hungrily dug into my share, slowly revelling in the delectable flavours.
The momo filling was dry and the skin, a bit thick and floury. Unlike the momos, which weren't really served hot, the soup was hot, clear and very soothing. I loved the Pork Hakka Chowmein which was absolutely delicious with lots of fresh vegetables, mild spices and small slices of pork. It contained the least amount of oil and a plate can be shared by two.
Then it was time for the best part, which really made our day. The Roast Chilli Pork, based on a slightly tangy sauce had some perfectly cooked pork slices with a fair amount of spice quotient. The crisp-skinned roasted pork with the succulent fat around the edges had the subtle hint of a smoky flavour that accentuated the richness of the dish. Combined with chillies, onions and bell peppers, the preparation was an instant hit! The Barbeque Pork was equally good with around 10 juicy and slightly chewy slices of the meat and we did not care to look up until the last morsels had vanished from our plates.

Overall, this is the best place for some awesome pork items at the cheapest rates. At this place, one can have a filling meal at even less than 100 rupees! I would highly recommend their Roast Chilli Pork and the Pork Hakka Chowmein to go with it.

P.S: Even if this is a better place for takeaways, my sit-in meal with friends was highly enjoyed. Sometimes, the surroundings get overshadowed by tasty authentic food at such low prices and Tibetan Delight proved how!

This was my first meet with the Calcutta Restaurants Facebook community as I was visiting Kolkata and got chance upon to be part of it. I arrived to find other foodies already taking their seats in an already cramped place which can only fit anything less than 25. I chanced upon an empty chair but the heat and the already over crowded place almost forced me out if it for some fresh air.

Since, I did a bit of research on the best dishes to order, I was prompt to order a plate of steamed chicken momo which was served soon, however without the clear soup. I did not bother to remind as I had already hogged them. Next on my wish list was chilly roasted pork which was promptly served too.

I was indecisive on the main course and wanted to a have a plate of pan fried chicken noodles with the white gravy. The waiter did not ask for the gravy options and instead reminded me that it would be spicy. I was little miffed as usually it is bland and needs additional sauce to spice it up. However, I let go the thoughts considering it might be a different variation.

To my utter surprise, I was served schezwan noodles and that too without the chicken. I verified if it was the chicken pan fried noodles, the waiter insisted. I started to have couple for spoons in search of the chicken. Alas! I couldn't find any and had to re-verify with the waiter who then scuffled through my plate of noodles and confirmed the chef has forgot to put the chicken pieces. He got hold of some boiled pieces of chicken and mixed it the noodles on my plate.

I felt a little disgusted as I was having high hopes and my sky high expectation on the food, was just inches above the ground. To level that was the utter disappointment with service. The food joint had information on the expected crowd turnout well ahead of the event but did not add to the service staff. The lone warrior was zapped by the barge of orders coming from the hunger mongers. The service quotient screwed up badly leaving a bad taste.

I hope they take note on the service part to cater on the larger crowd.

2013-07-17 16:21:06
Manjari Chowdhury
285678
3.0
These days there is a increased hullabaloo over 'ambiance'. Everywhere I go I hear 'ambiance' taking precedence over people's taste buds.  Now 'ambiance' is quite subjective , so while beautiful furniture, perfect lighting , excellent service, polite host, excellent food can all be marred by loud parties in your adjacent table and these days loud groups hog most of the restaurants with perfect ambiance but that can never be confused with hygiene and cleanliness which should be mandatory for all eateries. 

This tiny little place located inside a lane on Chowringee road  is wonderful for delightful takeaways. Locating it can be very tricky and had my friend not pointed it out on a previous visit to the area I wouldn't even have known where to peep in. Even then I would have missed it had I not seen two college going kids coming out of one tiny lane which reminded me of by-lanes of the Northern part of the city. once you start walking in there is a sign to direct you further inside the lane and you are greeted by some helping hands washing dishes in a small tiny courtyard. 

The little room serving food is dimly lit but the flooring makes it extremely dirty because of the modern tiles which become muddy very easily. There are a few small tables and so I decided to opt for takeaway. I ordered steamed pork momos, steamed rice with mixed gravy minus the prawns since I am highly allergic to prawns and chili roast pork. After having placed my order I noticed an empty table for two on the side of the entrance and decided to try a plate of pork kothay while I waited for my food. Having traveled extensively in the land of the momos my personal opinion is that while the dirt is a put of the food is delicious. The dough of the kothays was thin and perfect, the red meat was of a melt in the mouth texture . 

The only defect was that the filling was not enough for the dumpling. Either they should have reduced the size of the outer dough or they should increase the amount of filling. While I slowly tasted my food I found it difficult to eat it because of the dirty floor and so I looked around and was delighted to see Tibetan wooden wall hanging adorning the red walls and also that the peeling walls could do with a coating of paint. The lighting is perfect and the Tibetan lamps delighted someone such as myself who adores the mountains especially eastern Himalayan range. The roast chili pork is truly a delight. While it is not your usual melt in the mouth texture but quite succulent what sets it apart and gives its distinct flavour is its smoky taste. 

Their chili roast pork is a culinary addict's delight. As my fellow reviewer has pointed out the steamed rice with mixed gravy could do with a better serving proportion of gravy and since this easy dish can be tossed up anytime at home I would say it can be given a miss . My four dishes cost me only Rs335 and that indeed is a delight. That being said I must say that the meat in the gravy was soft and wonderful. So I would definitely not recommend visiting this place for a sit down meal but when one does get a hankering for Tibetan cuisine this place is the perfect one for takeaways. 

P.S. The Tibetan lady asked me how many people where there with me she greeted me with a very warm smile and invited me in. There has been quite a number of instances where the hosts have asked me with an unbelief in their voice if I was actually dining alone. also my rating for their food would be 4 out of 5 taking the cost into account but the overall rating would be 3 considering cleanliness , space etc.
